## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology (mathematical biology / population dynamics)
**Analysis**: The target dP_dt is an instantaneous population growth rate, naturally modeled by first-order population dynamics ODEs of the form dP_dt = f(P, t). With only (t, P) available, classical structures include density dependence in P, time-varying (seasonal/trending) intrinsic rates via t, and additive terms representing immigration/emigration or harvesting.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Malthusian (exponential) growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent per-capita growth)
- Constant immigration/emigration: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 (baseline net inflow/outflow independent of P)
- Proportional harvesting/mortality: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P (net rate reduced by proportional removal)
- Constant-yield harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 (fixed removal rate; can drive extinction at low P)
- Polynomial density dependence (generalized): dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (crowding or cooperation captured by nonlinear terms)
- Theta-logistic–type crowding (power crowding): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P**c2) (crowding strength scales as P**c2)
- Gompertz growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (logarithmic density regulation; multiplicative regulation in log-space)
- Ricker-type density dependence (exponential crowding): dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(-c1 * P) (per-capita growth decays approximately exponentially with P)
- Allee effect with crowding: dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 * P - 1) * (1 - c2 * P) (negative growth at low P plus high-P crowding)
- Beverton–Holt-type saturating regulation (continuous-time form): dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) - c2 * P (self-limitation via a saturating birth term plus linear loss)
- Seasonally forced per-capita rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P (periodic environment modulates growth rate)
- Trend + season forcing: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * t + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) * P (long-term drift with seasonal variability)
- Time-varying influx: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (immigration/emigration varying periodically)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Per-capita-rate modeling: if dP_dt scales roughly linearly with P, prefer structures like dP_dt = P * g(t, P) rather than purely additive forms.
- Crowding/self-limitation: observed slowing at high P is often captured by negative nonlinear terms in P (e.g., -P**2, -P**(1+c), or exp(-c*P) factors).
- Allee (low-density depensation): if growth is negative for small P but positive at intermediate P, include a factor like (c*P - 1) multiplying P.
- Log-regulation signature: if per-capita growth decreases roughly linearly with log(P), use P * log(c/P) (Gompertz-type).
- Seasonality: periodic oscillations in dP_dt at fixed P suggest sin(c*t + phase) modulating the per-capita rate.
- External forcing vs density effects: additive terms in dP_dt (e.g., +c0, +sin(c*t)) suggest immigration/stocking; multiplicative-on-P forcing suggests environment-driven birth/death rates.
- Extinction risk under harvesting: if trajectories show collapse below a threshold, include constant-yield removal (subtracting a constant) or strong Allee structure.
- Changing environment: monotone changes in growth behavior over time (even at similar P) suggest including linear or low-order polynomial trends in t inside the per-capita rate.

============================================================
GT Equivalence Verification (BPG14)
============================================================
GT: c0*(c1 - P/c2)*P + c3*(c4 - exp(-c5*P))*P + c6*P*exp(-c7*t)
Candidate formulas: 57

Let  
\[
GT(t,P)=a\Big[(1-\tfrac{P}{b})P+(1-e^{-kP})P+P e^{-kt}\Big]
\]
with fixed \(a=0.11423898258902421\), \(b=40.69810220267985\), \(k=0.08368363514073095\).

Expand the GT into “basis” terms:
\[
GT = a\Big(2P-\frac{1}{b}P^2 -P e^{-kP} + P e^{-kt}\Big).
\]
So any matching candidate must be able to represent **simultaneously** these four independent functional components in \((t,P)\):

1) \(P^2\) with coefficient \(-a/b\)  
2) \(P\) with coefficient \(2a\)  
3) \(P e^{-kP}\) with coefficient \(-a\) (note: exponential in **P** with a **negative** rate)  
4) \(P e^{-kt}\) with coefficient \(+a\) (note: exponential in **t** with a **negative** rate)  

Also, GT has **no** logs, sines/cosines, absolute values, rational \(P/(P+\cdot)\) terms, constants independent of \(P\), or exponentials like \(e^{+kP}\) or \(e^{+kt}\).

---

### Candidate-by-candidate analysis

**1.** \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2 e^{Pc3} + Pc4 e^{c5 t} + Pc6 + Pc7/(P+c8)\)  
Can set \(c3=-k\) to get \(P e^{-kP}\), and \(c5=-k\) to get \(P e^{-kt}\). But it also has an unavoidable rational term unless \(c7=0\). That’s fine. However it has **two separate linear-in-\(P\)** terms \(Pc1+Pc6\) (can combine) and can match \(2aP\). Also \(P^2c0\) matches \(-a/b P^2\). The only issue: GT needs **\(-a P e^{-kP}\)**, candidate provides \(+Pc2 e^{Pc3}\); choose \(c2=-a\), \(c3=-k\). And \(Pc4 e^{c5 t}\) choose \(c4=a\), \(c5=-k\). Works.  
✅ **Matches**.

**2.** \(P^2c0 + P^2c1 + Pc2 e^{Pc3} + Pc4 + Pc5 e^{c6 t} + Pc7/(Pc8+1)\)  
Can kill rational with \(c7=0\). Combine \(P^2\) terms into one coefficient. Set \(c3=-k\), \(c2=-a\). Set \(c6=-k\), \(c5=a\). Set \(c4=2a\). Set \(c0+c1=-a/b\).  
✅ **Matches**.

**3.** \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2 + Pc3 e^{Pc4} + Pc5 e^{c6 t} + Pc7 + Pc8/(Pc9+1)\)  
Has a **constant term** \(Pc2\) is linear (ok), but also \(Pc7\) linear (ok). Rational can be removed with \(c8=0\). Can set \(c4=-k\) and \(c3=-a\) to get \(-a P e^{-kP}\). Set \(c6=-k\), \(c5=a\). Set \(c0=-a/b\). Combine linear terms \(Pc1+Pc2+Pc7=2aP\).  
✅ **Matches**.

**4.** Like (3) but with rational \(P*c7/(Pc8+1)\) instead of \(Pc7\).  
To match GT, must remove rational by \(c7=0\). Then we lose one linear term but still have \(Pc1+Pc2\) to make \(2aP\). Other terms can match as in (3).  
✅ **Matches**.

**5.** Includes \(P c7 \log(1+c8/P)\) which cannot equal any GT basis term for all \(P\) unless \(c7=0\). If \(c7=0\), remaining terms: \(P^2\) terms, \(P e^{Pc3}\), constant-linear \(Pc4\), and \(P e^{c6 t}\). This can match GT exactly by choosing \(c3=-k\), \(c2=-a\), \(c6=-k\), \(c5=a\), \(c4=2a\), \(c0+c1=-a/b\).  
✅ **Matches** (with \(c7=0\)).

**6.** Has \(P c6 \log(1+c7/P)\) removable by \(c6=0\). Then same structure as (1) without rational; can match.  
✅ **Matches**.

**7.** Has \(P^{c6} c7 \log(Pc8+1)\): cannot reproduce GT terms unless coefficient is zero. Set \(c7=0\) to remove it. Remaining terms match as in (1).  
✅ **Matches**.

**8.** Has \(P^{c7}c8\log(c9|P|+1)\): must set \(c8=0\). Then remaining terms match as in (2).  
✅ **Matches**.

**9.** Has \(P c6 \log(c7/(P+1)+1)\) removable by \(c6=0\), but also has an additive constant \(+c8\) which must be 0. Then reduces to (1)-like and matches.  
✅ **Matches** (with \(c6=0,c8=0\)).

**10.** Contains \(P*c2/(P+c3)\) (a non-polynomial rational in \(P\)) and \(P*c4 e^{Pc5}\) and \(P^{c6}c7 e^{c8 t}\). You could set the rational term off by \(c2=0\). But then you have only **one** \(P e^{Pc5}\) term and **one** \(P^{c6} e^{c8 t}\) term; you can set \(c6=1\) to make it \(P e^{c8 t}\). However you still need both \(P\) and \(P^2\) and \(P e^{-kP}\) and \(P e^{-kt}\). You can get \(P^2\) and \(P\) from first two terms, \(P e^{-kP}\) from \(P*c4 e^{Pc5}\) (set \(c5=-k\), \(c4=-a\)), and \(P e^{-kt}\) from last term (set \(c6=1\), \(c7=a\), \(c8=-k\)). Works.  
✅ **Matches** (with \(c2=0\)).

**11.** Has constant \(+c7\) must be 0. Then same as (2) and matches.  
✅ **Matches**.

**12.** Has extra polynomial powers \(P*P^{c2}c3 = c3 P^{c2+1}\) and extra linear terms; can set unwanted ones to 0 by choosing coefficients 0. Keep \(P^2\) via \(P^2c0\) (and/or \(P^{c2+1}\) with \(c2=1\) but unnecessary). Need \(P e^{-kP}\): provided by \(P*c4 e^{Pc5}\) with \(c5=-k\), \(c4=-a\). Need \(P e^{-kt}\): provided by \(P*c7 e^{c8 t}\) with \(c7=a\), \(c8=-k\). Linear \(P\): combine \(P*c6 + P*c9\) etc to \(2aP\). Set other coefficients 0.  
✅ **Matches**.

```
0.11424*(1 - P/40.698)*P + 0.11424*(1 - exp(-0.08368*P))*P + 0.11424*P*exp(-0.08368*t)

Expanding:
```
0.11424*P - 0.11424*P²/40.698 + 0.11424*P - 0.11424*P*exp(-0.08368*P) + 0.11424*P*exp(-0.08368*t)

```

```
